"""Triton-based paged attention decode kernel for packed KV cache layout.

The KV cache is laid out as (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2)
with K and V packed on the last dimension: [K | V].

This kernel uses a two-stage approach:
1. Stage 1 splits the KV sequence into NUM_KV_SPLITS parts, each block computes
   partial attention with online softmax.
2. Stage 2 reduces partial results across splits.

For efficiency on the packed layout, each iteration loads K and V separately
using coalesced per-token loads.
"""
import math

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import triton
import triton.language as tl

OP_TYPE = "attention"
SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]

BATCH = 8
NUM_HEADS = 32
NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
HEAD_DIM = 128
SEQ_LEN = 1024
PAGE_SIZE = 16


# --------------------------------------------------------------------------- #
# Stage 1: compute partial attention per KV split (grouped for GQA)
# --------------------------------------------------------------------------- #
@triton.jit
def _fwd_kernel_stage1(
    Q,
    KV_Cache,
    block_table,
    seq_lens,
    sm_scale,
    Mid_O,
    stride_qb,
    stride_qh,
    stride_bt0,
    stride_bt1,
    stride_kv0,
    stride_kv1,
    stride_kv2,
    stride_kv3,
    stride_mid_ob,
    stride_mid_oh,
    stride_mid_os,
    kv_group_num: tl.constexpr,
    q_head_num: tl.constexpr,
    BLOCK_DMODEL: tl.constexpr,
    BLOCK_DV: tl.constexpr,
    BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr,
    NUM_KV_SPLITS: tl.constexpr,
    PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
    HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
):
    cur_batch = tl.program_id(0)
    cur_head_id = tl.program_id(1)
    split_kv_id = tl.program_id(2)

    # Which KV head this group belongs to
    heads_per_kv = tl.cdiv(kv_group_num, BLOCK_H)
    cur_kv_head = cur_head_id // heads_per_kv

    # Number of valid query heads in this block
    if kv_group_num > BLOCK_H:
        VALID_BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr = BLOCK_H
    else:
        VALID_BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr = kv_group_num

    cur_head = cur_head_id * VALID_BLOCK_H + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_H)
    mask_h = cur_head < (cur_head_id + 1) * VALID_BLOCK_H
    mask_h = mask_h & (cur_head < q_head_num)

    offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_DMODEL)
    offs_dv = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_DV)
    mask_d = offs_d < HEAD_DIM
    mask_dv = offs_dv < HEAD_DIM

    cur_batch_seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens + cur_batch)

    # Load Q for this head group
    offs_q = cur_batch * stride_qb + cur_head[:, None] * stride_qh + offs_d[None, :]
    q = tl.load(Q + offs_q, mask=mask_h[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0)

    # Determine this split's token range
    kv_len_per_split = tl.cdiv(cur_batch_seq_len, NUM_KV_SPLITS)
    split_kv_start = kv_len_per_split * split_kv_id
    split_kv_end = tl.minimum(split_kv_start + kv_len_per_split, cur_batch_seq_len)

    # Online softmax accumulators
    e_max = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H], dtype=tl.float32) - float("inf")
    e_sum = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H], dtype=tl.float32)
    acc = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H, BLOCK_DV], dtype=tl.float32)

    if split_kv_end > split_kv_start:
        # Iterate over pages within this split
        start_page = split_kv_start // PAGE_SIZE
        end_page = (split_kv_end + PAGE_SIZE - 1) // PAGE_SIZE

        offs_token_in_page = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)

        for page_idx in range(start_page, end_page):
            physical_page = tl.load(
                block_table + cur_batch * stride_bt0 + page_idx * stride_bt1,
            )

            # Global token indices for this page
            global_token_idx = page_idx * PAGE_SIZE + offs_token_in_page
            token_mask = global_token_idx < split_kv_end

            # Base address for this page and KV head
            page_base = (
                KV_Cache
                + physical_page * stride_kv0
                + cur_kv_head * stride_kv2
            )

            # Load K and V separately (packed layout: [K|V] on last dim)
            k = tl.load(
                page_base + offs_token_in_page[:, None] * stride_kv1 + offs_d[None, :],
                mask=token_mask[:, None] & mask_d[None, :],
                other=0.0,
            )
            v = tl.load(
                page_base + offs_token_in_page[:, None] * stride_kv1 + (HEAD_DIM + offs_dv)[None, :],
                mask=token_mask[:, None] & mask_dv[None, :],
                other=0.0,
            )

            # Compute QK^T
            qk = tl.dot(q, k.to(q.dtype).T)
            qk *= sm_scale

            # Mask tokens beyond split end or seq_len
            qk = tl.where(
                mask_h[:, None] & token_mask[None, :],
                qk,
                float("-inf"),
            )

            # Online softmax update
            n_e_max = tl.maximum(tl.max(qk, 1), e_max)
            re_scale = tl.exp(e_max - n_e_max)
            p = tl.exp(qk - n_e_max[:, None])

            acc *= re_scale[:, None]
            acc += tl.dot(p.to(v.dtype), v)

            e_sum = e_sum * re_scale + tl.sum(p, 1)
            e_max = n_e_max

        # Store partial output and LSE
        offs_mid_o = (
            cur_batch * stride_mid_ob
            + cur_head[:, None] * stride_mid_oh
            + split_kv_id * stride_mid_os
            + offs_dv[None, :]
        )
        tl.store(
            Mid_O + offs_mid_o,
            acc / e_sum[:, None],
            mask=mask_h[:, None] & mask_dv[None, :],
        )

        offs_mid_lse = (
            cur_batch * stride_mid_ob
            + cur_head * stride_mid_oh
            + split_kv_id * stride_mid_os
            + HEAD_DIM
        )
        tl.store(
            Mid_O + offs_mid_lse,
            e_max + tl.log(e_sum),
            mask=mask_h,
        )


# --------------------------------------------------------------------------- #
# Stage 2: reduce partial results across KV splits
# --------------------------------------------------------------------------- #
@triton.jit
def _fwd_kernel_stage2(
    Mid_O,
    O,
    seq_lens,
    stride_mid_ob,
    stride_mid_oh,
    stride_mid_os,
    stride_obs,
    stride_oh,
    NUM_KV_SPLITS: tl.constexpr,
    BLOCK_DV: tl.constexpr,
    HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
):
    cur_batch = tl.program_id(0)
    cur_head = tl.program_id(1)

    cur_batch_seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens + cur_batch)

    offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_DV)
    mask_d = offs_d < HEAD_DIM

    e_sum = 0.0
    e_max = -float("inf")
    acc = tl.zeros([BLOCK_DV], dtype=tl.float32)

    offs_v = cur_batch * stride_mid_ob + cur_head * stride_mid_oh + offs_d
    offs_lse = cur_batch * stride_mid_ob + cur_head * stride_mid_oh + HEAD_DIM

    for split_kv_id in range(0, NUM_KV_SPLITS):
        split_kv_start = tl.cdiv(cur_batch_seq_len, NUM_KV_SPLITS) * split_kv_id
        split_kv_end = tl.minimum(
            split_kv_start + tl.cdiv(cur_batch_seq_len, NUM_KV_SPLITS),
            cur_batch_seq_len,
        )

        if split_kv_end > split_kv_start:
            tv = tl.load(
                Mid_O + offs_v + split_kv_id * stride_mid_os,
                mask=mask_d,
                other=0.0,
            )
            tlogic = tl.load(Mid_O + offs_lse + split_kv_id * stride_mid_os)
            n_e_max = tl.maximum(tlogic, e_max)

            old_scale = tl.exp(e_max - n_e_max)
            acc *= old_scale
            exp_logic = tl.exp(tlogic - n_e_max)
            acc += exp_logic * tv

            e_sum = e_sum * old_scale + exp_logic
            e_max = n_e_max

    tl.store(
        O + cur_batch * stride_obs + cur_head * stride_oh + offs_d,
        acc / e_sum,
        mask=mask_d,
    )


# --------------------------------------------------------------------------- #
# Python wrappers
# --------------------------------------------------------------------------- #
def _decode_grouped_att_m_fwd(
    q,
    kv_cache,
    block_table,
    seq_lens,
    mid_o,
    num_kv_splits,
    sm_scale,
    page_size,
    BLOCK_H: int = 8,
):
    batch, head_num = q.shape[0], q.shape[1]
    num_kv_heads = kv_cache.shape[2]
    head_dim = kv_cache.shape[3] // 2
    kv_group_num = head_num // num_kv_heads

    # Correct grid: each "head group" covers up to BLOCK_H query heads that
    # map to the same KV head.  We must divide by min(BLOCK_H, kv_group_num)
    # so that every KV head gets its own set of blocks.
    grid = (
        batch,
        triton.cdiv(head_num, min(BLOCK_H, kv_group_num)),
        num_kv_splits,
    )

    BLOCK_DMODEL = triton.next_power_of_2(head_dim)
    BLOCK_DV = triton.next_power_of_2(head_dim)

    stride_kv = kv_cache.stride()
    stride_bt = block_table.stride()

    _fwd_kernel_stage1[grid](
        q,
        kv_cache,
        block_table,
        seq_lens,
        sm_scale,
        mid_o,
        q.stride(0),
        q.stride(1),
        stride_bt[0],
        stride_bt[1],
        stride_kv[0],
        stride_kv[1],
        stride_kv[2],
        stride_kv[3],
        mid_o.stride(0),
        mid_o.stride(1),
        mid_o.stride(2),
        kv_group_num=kv_group_num,
        q_head_num=head_num,
        BLOCK_DMODEL=BLOCK_DMODEL,
        BLOCK_DV=BLOCK_DV,
        BLOCK_H=BLOCK_H,
        NUM_KV_SPLITS=num_kv_splits,
        PAGE_SIZE=page_size,
        HEAD_DIM=head_dim,
        num_warps=4,
        num_stages=2,
    )


def _decode_softmax_reducev_fwd(
    mid_o,
    o,
    seq_lens,
    num_kv_splits,
):
    batch, head_num = o.shape[0], o.shape[1]
    head_dim = o.shape[2]
    BLOCK_DV = triton.next_power_of_2(head_dim)

    grid = (batch, head_num)
    _fwd_kernel_stage2[grid](
        mid_o,
        o,
        seq_lens,
        mid_o.stride(0),
        mid_o.stride(1),
        mid_o.stride(2),
        o.stride(0),
        o.stride(1),
        NUM_KV_SPLITS=num_kv_splits,
        BLOCK_DV=BLOCK_DV,
        HEAD_DIM=head_dim,
        num_warps=4,
        num_stages=2,
    )


def paged_attention_decode(
    query,
    kv_cache,
    block_table,
    seq_lens,
    sm_scale,
    page_size,
    num_kv_splits,
):
    batch, num_heads, head_dim = query.shape

    # Intermediate buffers for stage 1 -> stage 2
    # Layout: (batch, num_heads, num_kv_splits, head_dim+1)
    # Last element of each slice stores LSE
    mid_o = torch.empty(
        (batch, num_heads, num_kv_splits, head_dim + 1),
        dtype=torch.float32,
        device=query.device,
    )

    output = torch.empty_like(query)

    _decode_grouped_att_m_fwd(
        query,
        kv_cache,
        block_table,
        seq_lens,
        mid_o,
        num_kv_splits,
        sm_scale,
        page_size,
    )
    _decode_softmax_reducev_fwd(
        mid_o,
        output,
        seq_lens,
        num_kv_splits,
    )

    return output


# --------------------------------------------------------------------------- #
# Model interface
# --------------------------------------------------------------------------- #
class Model(nn.Module):
    def __init__(
        self,
        batch: int,
        num_heads: int,
        num_kv_heads: int,
        head_dim: int,
        seq_len: int,
        page_size: int,
    ):
        super().__init__()
        assert num_heads % num_kv_heads == 0
        self.batch = batch
        self.num_heads = num_heads
        self.num_kv_heads = num_kv_heads
        self.head_dim = head_dim
        self.seq_len = seq_len
        self.page_size = page_size
        self.group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads
        self.scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim)

        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.bfloat16), persistent=False)

    def forward(
        self,
        query: torch.Tensor,
        kv_cache: torch.Tensor,
        block_table: torch.Tensor,
        seq_lens: torch.Tensor,
    ) -> torch.Tensor:
        # Heuristic: use more KV splits when the sequence is longer or when
        # there are fewer query heads (low natural occupancy).  More splits
        # increase the number of stage-1 blocks and improve parallelism.
        max_seq_len = self.seq_len

        # Target a total stage-1 block count that keeps the GPU well occupied.
        # With smaller head_dim each block does less work per page, so we need
        # more blocks (hence more splits) to hide latency.
        head_groups = (self.num_heads + min(8, self.group_size) - 1) // min(8, self.group_size)
        base_blocks = self.batch * head_groups
        target_blocks = 640 if self.head_dim <= 64 else 512
        num_kv_splits = max(1, min(24, target_blocks // base_blocks))

        return paged_attention_decode(
            query,
            kv_cache,
            block_table,
            seq_lens,
            self.scale,
            self.page_size,
            num_kv_splits,
        )


def get_inputs():
    B = BATCH
    H = NUM_HEADS
    Hkv = NUM_KV_HEADS
    D = HEAD_DIM
    L = SEQ_LEN
    P = PAGE_SIZE

    pages_per_seq = (L + P - 1) // P
    total_pages = max(B * pages_per_seq + 8, 64)

    query = torch.randn(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    kv_cache = torch.randn(total_pages, P, Hkv, 2 * D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1

    perm = torch.randperm(total_pages)[: B * pages_per_seq].reshape(B, pages_per_seq).int()
    block_table = perm.contiguous()
    seq_lens = torch.full((B,), L, dtype=torch.int32)

    return [query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens]


def get_init_inputs():
    return [BATCH, NUM_HEADS, NUM_KV_HEADS, HEAD_DIM, SEQ_LEN, PAGE_SIZE]

     1	"""Naive PyTorch paged-attention decode reference (correctness oracle, not SOTA).
     2	
     3	Single-query decode: each batch element has a query of shape (num_heads, head_dim)
     4	and attends over a KV cache of `seq_len[b]` tokens stored as fixed-size pages in
     5	a global pool. Pages for batch element b are listed in `block_table[b]`.
     6	
     7	The reference performs the slow path:
     8	  1. Gather pages -> contiguous (seq_len, num_kv_heads, head_dim) per batch element.
     9	  2. Repeat KV heads for grouped-query (broadcast num_kv_heads -> num_heads).
    10	  3. Manual softmax(QK^T / sqrt(d)) @ V in fp32, cast back to bf16.
    11	
    12	This avoids torch.nn.functional.scaled_dot_product_attention (which is on the
    13	forbidden list) so the agent cannot dispatch through SDPA either.
    14	"""
    15	import math
    16	
    17	import torch
    18	import torch.nn as nn
    19	
    20	OP_TYPE = "attention"
    21	SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]

     1	name: 03_paged_attention
     2	display_name: "Paged Attention Decode"
     3	precision: bf16
     4	regime: memory  # decode is bandwidth-bound (KV cache streamed once per token)
     5	
     6	# Effective FLOPs per call: QK^T + softmax*V across all batches/heads/seq.
     7	# Sum-formula evaluated per-shape; the benchmark substitutes batch/num_heads/etc.
     8	# 2 * B * H * L * D for QK^T plus 2 * B * H * L * D for AV  =>  4 * B * H * L * D
     9	flops_formula: "4 * batch * num_heads * seq_len * head_dim"
    10	
    11	# Bytes moved (the real bottleneck): the KV cache must be streamed end-to-end.
    12	#   K and V each:  batch * seq_len * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2 bytes (bf16)
    13	#   Q: batch * num_heads * head_dim * 2  (negligible vs KV)
    14	#   Out: same as Q
    15	# So total ~ 2 * (B * L * Hkv * D * 2) + small.
    16	bytes_formula: "2 * batch * seq_len * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2 + batch * num_heads * head_dim * 2 * 2"

The kernel goes in solution.py with same interface as reference.py This is a memory-bound operation. The key to performance is: - Efficient memory access patterns for the paged KV cache - Good thread-level parallelism - Handling GQA (grouped query attention) efficiently - Handling non-power-of-2 seq_lens For a decode kernel, the best approach is typically: 1. **Triton** - Easier to write, good for decode attention kernels 2. **CUDA C++** via load_inline - More control, potentially faster For Blackwell/SM120, I need to be careful about what features are available. Triton is likely the most practical approach for quickly iterating and getting good performance. Let me think about the algorithm: For paged attention decode: - Each batch element has 1 query token - Query shape: (batch, num_heads, head_dim) - KV cache is paged: (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim*2) - block_table tells which pages belong to which sequence - seq_lens tells actual sequence length The standard approach for decode attention is: 1. For each head, load the query vector 2. Iterate through KV pages, loading K and V 3. Compute Q*K^T scores 4. Online softmax 5. Accumulate weighted V values For GQA, multiple query heads share the same KV head. We can compute the scores for all query heads in a group simultaneously. reasoning (4087 chars)
Good, we have: - PyTorch 2.11.0 with CUDA 13.0 - RTX PRO 6000 Blackwell, SM120 (12, 0) - Triton 3.6.0 This is a very new Blackwell GPU. Triton 3.6 should have some Blackwell support, but I need to be careful. For a paged attention decode kernel, the standard approach in Triton is: 1. Use one block per (batch element, query head) or per (batch element, query head group) 2. Each block loads the query vector once 3. Iterates through the KV cache pages, computing QK^T and accumulating weighted V 4. Uses online softmax for numerical stability Let me look at the vLLM Triton kernel or FlashInfer's implementation for reference. Let me also check if there's a vllm triton kernel available locally. Actually, let me just write a Triton kernel. For decode attention with GQA, the key optimization points are: 1. **GMEM coalescing**: Load KV cache in a coalesced manner 2. **Shared memory usage**: Cache Q and intermediate results 3. **GQA handling**: Process multiple Q heads per KV head in parallel 4. **Warp-level parallelism**: Use efficient dot products For Blackwell specifically: - FP8/BF16 tensor cores are very fast - We want to maximize memory bandwidth utilization since decode is memory-bound Let me think about the kernel design: **Kernel 1 (QK^T scores + online softmax)**: - Each thread block handles one (batch, query_head) - Threads within a block cooperate to iterate over the KV sequence - We load K vectors from paged memory, compute dot product with Q - Use online softmax to track max and sum_exp **Kernel 2 (weighted V accumulation)**: - Actually, we can do this in a single pass with online softmax Let me write a fused kernel that does everything in one pass. The standard algorithm: ``` for each token t in sequence: score = dot(Q, K[t]) score = score * scale max_score = max(max_score, score) exp_score = exp(score - max_score) sum_exp = sum_exp * exp(old_max - max_score) + exp_score out = out * exp(old_max - max_score) + exp_score * V[t] ``` Wait, that's not quite right for the online softmax. Let me use the standard streaming softmax: ``` m = -inf l = 0 o = 0 for each chunk: s = q @ k_chunk^T m_new = max(m, max(s)) p = exp(s - m_new) l = l * exp(m - m_new) + sum(p) o = o * exp(m - m_new) + p @ v_chunk m = m_new ``` For a single query, this simplifies. Each token produces one score. For the kernel layout: - One thread block per (batch element, query head) is simple but may not have enough parallelism - For GQA with group_size = 4, we could have one block handle all 4 query heads that share the same KV head - This amortizes KV loads across the group Let me think about optimal thread block configuration: - For head_dim=128, we can use 128 threads (one per element) - For head_dim=64, we can use 64 threads or 128 threads - We want to process the sequence in chunks Actually, for decode, the standard Triton approach is: - Each thread block handles one query head - Threads are arranged to load K/V efficiently - We iterate through pages, loading K and V for each token Since the page_size is 16 and head_dim is 128, each K or V page-block is 16 * 128 * 2 = 4096 bytes for one KV head. With GQA group_size=4, we need to load this once and compute 4 dot products. For batch=32, num_heads=32, this gives 1024 thread blocks. Each thread block processes seq_len=2048 tokens. At 1.8 TB/s, reading K+V is about 2 * 2048 * 8 * 128 * 2 = 8.4 MB per batch, or about 4.6 us at peak bandwidth. But we have 1024 blocks, so we need to be efficient. Let me write a Triton kernel. I'll structure it as follows: 1. One block per (batch, query_head) for simplicity first 2. Each block loads its query vector into shared memory 3. Iterates over pages using block_table 4. For each page, loads K and V vectors 5. Computes scores, online softmax, and accumulates output Actually, let me first look at an existing Triton kernel for decode attention to make sure I get the details right. Let me search for vLLM's Triton kernel or a similar implementation. Let me check what's in the environment first.

This is very helpful! The vLLM triton_decode_attention.py gives me a great template. Let me analyze it: 1. It uses a 2-stage approach: - Stage 1: Split KV sequence into `NUM_KV_SPLITS` parts, each block processes one (batch, head, split) and computes partial attention with online softmax - Stage 2: Reduce the partial results across splits 2. For GQA, it uses `_fwd_grouped_kernel_stage1` which processes multiple query heads per block using `tl.dot` 3. The KV cache layout is different from ours though - their `K_Buffer` and `V_Buffer` are separate tensors with layout `(..., PAGE_SIZE, NUM_HEADS, HEAD_DIM)`, while ours is `(num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2)` with K and V packed. I need to adapt this to our layout. Let me also look at how they handle the paged memory access: - `kv_page_number = tl.load(Req_to_tokens + stride_req_to_tokens_b * cur_batch_req_idx + offs_n // PAGE_SIZE)` - `kv_loc = kv_page_number * PAGE_SIZE + offs_n % PAGE_SIZE` - Then `offs_buf_k = kv_loc[:, None] * stride_buf_kbs + cur_kv_head * stride_buf_kh + offs_d[None, :]` For our layout: - `kv_cache` is `(num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2)` - `block_table[b]` gives the page indices for batch b - Each page has shape `(page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2)` So for token index `n` in batch `b`: - `page_idx = block_table[b, n // page_size]` - `offset_in_page = n % page_size` - `k = kv_cache[page_idx, offset_in_page, kv_head, :head_dim]` - `v = kv_cache[page_idx, offset_in_page, kv_head, head_dim:]` The stride would be: - `stride_nblocks = page_size * num_kv_heads * (2 * head_dim)` for moving between blocks - `stride_page = num_kv_heads * (2 * head_dim)` for moving within a page - `stride_kvhead = 2 * head_dim` for moving between kv heads - Or more simply, we can just compute linear indices Now, the vLLM kernel expects K and V as separate buffers. In our case, they're packed. We have two options: 1. Split K and V at the Python level before calling the kernel 2. Access the packed buffer directly in the kernel Option 2 is more efficient (less memory, no preprocessing). Let me write a kernel that accesses the packed KV cache directly. Actually, looking at our problem constraints, the forbidden ops are just vllm.attention, flashinfer, SDPA. I can freely write a Triton kernel. No logit_cap, no alibi slopes For performance on Blackwell, I want: - Good memory coalescing when reading KV cache - Efficient use of tensor cores if possible (but for decode, it's mostly memory-bound) - Minimal overhead For the packed layout, the K and V for a given (page, token_in_page, kv_head) are contiguous in memory: - `kv_cache[page, token, kv_head, :head_dim]` = K - `kv_cache[page, token, kv_head, head_dim:]` = V The stride structure: - stride_0 = page_size * num_kv_heads * (2 * head_dim) # between blocks - stride_1 = num_kv_heads * (2 * head_dim) # within a page - stride_2 = 2 * head_dim # between kv heads - stride_3 = 1 # within head_dim Actually, in the Triton kernel, I'll compute offsets directly using the strides. 188 SMs on Blackwell. That's a lot. For batch=4, num_heads=64, seq_len=4096: - Total thread blocks = 4 * 64 = 256 for single-pass - That's more than 188, so it's enough to occupy the GPU, but each block has a lot of work (4096 tokens) For batch=8, num_heads=16, seq_len=2000: - Total blocks = 8 * 16 = 128 - Less than 188, might not fully occupy For batch=16, num_heads=32, seq_len=1535: - Total blocks = 16 * 32 = 512 - Plenty So for some shapes, single-pass might not fully utilize the GPU. But for decode attention, the bottleneck is memory bandwidth, not compute. So occupancy is less critical than good memory access patterns. Actually, wait - with 188 SMs, each running a warp, that's a lot of parallelism. And decode attention is very memory-bound, so the key is saturating memory bandwidth, not having thousands of blocks. Let me think about what limits memory bandwidth utilization: 1. Coalesced loads of KV cache 2. Hiding latency through warps per SM 3. Minimizing shared memory pressure For our packed layout `(num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2)`: - Loading K for one token and one head: contiguous `head_dim` elements (128 for D=128, 64 for D=64) - Loading V immediately after: also contiguous `head_dim` elements - For page_size=16 and head_dim=128, one page for one kv_head has K+V of 16 * 128 * 2 * 2 = 8192 bytes If a warp loads 32 tokens at a time (BLOCK_N=32), that's 32 * 128 * 2 * 2 = 16384 bytes for K+V per head. Actually, looking at the vLLM kernel more carefully, they use BLOCK_N=64 for non-HIP and BLOCK_N=32 for grouped. Let me check why. In `_decode_att_m_fwd` (non-grouped): - BLOCK = 64 - num_warps = 4 In `_decode_grouped_att_m_fwd` (grouped): - BLOCK = 32 - num_warps = 4 For grouped with BLOCK_H=16, each block processes 16 query heads against 32 tokens. The shared memory usage: - Q: 16 * 128 * 2 = 4096 bytes - K: 32 * 128 * 2 = 8192 bytes - V: 32 * 128 * 2 = 8192 bytes - Total: ~20KB, well within limits For head_dim=64: - Q: 16 * 64 * 2 = 2048 bytes - K: 32 * 64 * 2 = 4096 bytes - V: 32 * 64 * 2 = 4096 bytes - Total: ~10KB So shared memory is not an issue. Now, for the actual kernel design. Let me write a Triton kernel that: 1. Handles our packed KV cache layout 2. Uses grouped query attention 3. Handles variable sequence lengths 4. Optionally uses 2-stage reduction for better parallelism on long sequences Let me start with a single-stage kernel for simplicity, then optimize. Actually, let me think about performance more carefully. For decode attention on a memory-bound workload: The total memory read per forward pass: - K cache: batch * seq_len * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2 bytes - V cache: same - Q: batch * num_heads * head_dim * 2 bytes (negligible) - Output: batch * num_heads * head_dim * 2 bytes (negligible) For shape 2: batch=32, num_kv_heads=8, head_dim=128, seq_len=2048 - K+V = 32 * 2048 * 8 * 128 * 2 * 2 = 268,435,456 bytes = 256 MB - At 1.8 TB/s = 1800 GB/s, this takes 256 / 1800 = 0.142 ms So the theoretical minimum is about 0.14 ms for the largest shape. We need to get close to this. Let me write a kernel now. I'll base it on the vLLM approach but adapt it to our layout. For stage 1, I'll write a kernel that: - Takes packed KV cache - Computes partial attention for each KV split - Stores intermediate results For stage 2: - Reduces across splits Let me also think about whether to split K and V at the Python level. If I split them, I can reuse more of the vLLM kernel structure. But splitting requires an extra copy. For a single forward pass, that's extra overhead. Actually, I can just pass the same tensor pointer with different offsets for K and V. The kernel can compute: - K offset: `base + 0` - V offset: `base + head_dim` So I don't need to split, I just need one buffer pointer and use different offsets. Let me write the solution now. Still decent. For smaller shapes, the copy overhead is proportionally smaller or similar. Actually, I can do better. For loading a page: ```python offs_token = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)[:, None] # (16, 1) offs_dim = tl.arange(0, 2 * HEAD_DIM)[None, :] # (1, 256) page_data = tl.load(page_base + offs_token * stride_kv1 + offs_dim) ``` Thread (t, d) accesses `page_base + t * stride_kv1 + d`. Since stride_kv1 = num_kv_heads * 2 * HEAD_DIM, and `d` varies fastest in the thread layout (rightmost index varies fastest), threads in a warp access consecutive `d` values for the same `t`. That's `page_base + t * stride_kv1 + d`, `page_base + t * stride_kv1 + d+1`, etc. This is perfectly coalesced! A warp of 32 threads accesses 32 consecutive elements in the `d` dimension. For `2*HEAD_DIM=256`, the first 8 warps cover the full 256 elements for `t=0`, the next 8 warps cover `t=1`, etc. Actually, it depends on how threads are mapped. In Triton, for a block of shape (16, 256), threads are arranged in row-major order: the rightmost dimension varies fastest. So: - Thread 0: (0, 0) - Thread 1: (0, 1) - ... - Thread 31: (0, 31) - Thread 32: (0, 32) - ... If we have 128 threads (4 warps), they cover (0, 0..127) in the first warp, (0, 128..255) in the second warp, (1, 0..127) in the third warp, (1, 128..255) in the fourth warp. Wait, I need to check how Triton maps threads to block elements. For a block shape (M, N), Triton creates a 1D thread index `i` and maps it to `(i // N, i % N)` or similar. So for (16, 256): - Thread 0: (0, 0) - Thread 1: (0, 1) - ... - Thread 255: (0, 255) - Thread 256: (1, 0) - ... With 128 threads per block, in each iteration the block loads elements: - Iteration 0: threads 0..127 load (0, 0..127) - Iteration 1: threads 0..127 load (0, 128..255) - Iteration 2: threads 0..127 load (1, 0..127) - etc. Wait, no. Triton doesn't iterate like that for loads. A `tl.load` of shape (16, 256) with 128 threads would have each thread load 32 elements? Or does each thread load one element and Triton figures out the vectorization? Actually, Triton automatically vectorizes loads. For a block of shape (16, 256), Triton might use 128-bit loads (8 bf16 elements) per thread. With 128 threads, that's 1024 elements per instruction, so it would take multiple instructions. The key point is: threads in a warp access consecutive memory addresses. For (16, 256), a warp of 32 threads accesses 32 consecutive elements in the N dimension. So warp 0 accesses (0, 0..31), warp 1 accesses (0, 32..63), etc. Each warp's access is perfectly coalesced into one or two 128-byte cache lines. So loading a full page is very efficient! After loading, `page_data[:, :HEAD_DIM]` extracts K. In Triton, this is just referencing a subset of the loaded registers. Similarly for V. Then `tl.dot(q, k.T)` where k is (PAGE_SIZE, HEAD_DIM): - q is (BLOCK_H, BLOCK_DMODEL) = (16, 128) - k.T is (128, 16) - tl.dot produces (16, 16) This should use tensor cores efficiently. Great! Let me write this kernel now. One more consideration: `page_data[:, :HEAD_DIM]` - I need to make sure Triton handles this correctly. Let me test it. Actually, I just realized there might be an issue with `tl.dot(q, k.T)` when k comes from slicing. In Triton, does the slice maintain the right layout for dot product? I believe so, because Triton blocks are always row-major, and `k.T` transposes to col-major for the dot product. But `k` is shape (PAGE_SIZE, HEAD_DIM), so `k.T` is shape (HEAD_DIM, PAGE_SIZE). `tl.dot(q, k.T)` where q is (BLOCK_H, BLOCK_DMODEL) and BLOCK_DMODEL = HEAD_DIM (for power-of-2 head_dim). The inner dimensions match: BLOCK_DMODEL = HEAD_DIM. Let me also handle the non-power-of-2 head_dim case. The shapes only have head_dim=128 and head_dim=64, both power-of-2. So BLOCK_DMODEL = HEAD_DIM always. Wait, what about the mask? When loading a page, some tokens might be beyond seq_len. The `tl.load` mask ensures we don't read out-of-bounds memory. But for the last page, if it's partial, we load the full page and mask the extra tokens when computing qk. ```python token_mask = offs_token + page_idx * PAGE_SIZE < cur_batch_seq_len qk = tl.where(token_mask[None, :], qk, float("-inf")) ``` This ensures extra tokens contribute -inf to softmax, effectively zeroing them out. For V accumulation, the extra tokens have p=0 (because exp(-inf)=0), so they don't contribute to the output. One more thing: I should be careful about `tl.load` with mask on the page_data. For tokens beyond seq_len in the last page, we might read garbage data. But since those tokens are masked in qk and p, they don't affect the output. However, reading out-of-bounds memory could cause a segfault if the page is at the edge of allocated memory. Wait, in our test setup, all pages are fully allocated. The `kv_cache` has shape `(num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, 2*head_dim)`. Even if we only use 15 tokens out of a 16-token page, reading the 16th token is within the allocated memory. So it's safe. But we should still mask the load if we're worried about NaNs or something. Actually, for the last page, we might read whatever random data is in the unused token slot. But since we mask qk to -inf for those tokens, the softmax handles it correctly. However, if the garbage data contains NaN, `tl.dot` might propagate NaN. To be safe, I'll mask the load: ```python page_data = tl.load( page_base + offs_token[:, None] * stride_kv1 + offs_dim[None, :], mask=token_mask[:, None], other=0.0 ) ``` This loads 0.0 for unused tokens. Then k=0 and v=0 for those tokens. qk for those tokens will be 0, but we still need to set them to -inf: ```python qk = tl.where(token_mask[None, :], qk, float("-inf")) ``` Wait, if k=0, then qk=0, and exp(0)=1, which would contribute to the softmax. That's wrong! I must set qk=-inf for masked tokens regardless of what k is. So: ```python qk = tl.dot(q, k.T) * sm_scale qk = tl.where(token_mask[None, :], qk, float("-inf")) ``` This is correct. The masked tokens get -inf score, so p=0 for them. But we also want v=0 for masked tokens to avoid NaN issues. Since we mask the load with `other=0.0`, v is already 0 for masked tokens. Good. OK, let me write the actual code now. I'll create a complete solution.py.

+"""Triton-based paged attention decode kernel for packed KV cache layout.
+
+The KV cache is laid out as (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2)
+with K and V packed on the last dimension: [K | V].
+
+This kernel uses a two-stage approach:
+1. Stage 1 splits the KV sequence into NUM_KV_SPLITS parts, each block computes
+   partial attention with online softmax.
+2. Stage 2 reduces partial results across splits.
+
+For efficiency on the packed layout, each iteration loads an entire page
+(page_size tokens x 2*head_dim elements) as a coalesced block, then extracts
+K and V slices.
+"""
+import math
+
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+OP_TYPE = "attention"
+SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
+HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]
+
+BATCH = 8
+NUM_HEADS = 32
+NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
+HEAD_DIM = 128
+SEQ_LEN = 1024
+PAGE_SIZE = 16
+
+
+# --------------------------------------------------------------------------- #
+# Stage 1: compute partial attention per KV split (grouped for GQA)
+# --------------------------------------------------------------------------- #
+@triton.jit
+def _fwd_kernel_stage1(
+    Q,
+    KV_Cache,
+    block_table,
+    seq_lens,
+    sm_scale,
+    Mid_O,
+    Mid_LSE,
+    stride_qb,
+    stride_qh,
+    stride_bt0,
+    stride_bt1,
+    stride_kv0,
+    stride_kv1,
+    stride_kv2,
+    stride_kv3,
+    stride_mid_ob,
+    stride_mid_oh,
+    stride_mid_os,
+    kv_group_num: tl.constexpr,
+    q_head_num: tl.constexpr,
+    BLOCK_DMODEL: tl.constexpr,
+    BLOCK_DV: tl.constexpr,
+    BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr,
+    NUM_KV_SPLITS: tl.constexpr,
+    PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+    HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    cur_batch = tl.program_id(0)
+    cur_head_id = tl.program_id(1)
+    split_kv_id = tl.program_id(2)
+
+    # Which KV head this group belongs to
+    heads_per_kv = tl.cdiv(kv_group_num, BLOCK_H)
+    cur_kv_head = cur_head_id // heads_per_kv
+
+    # Number of valid query heads in this block
+    if kv_group_num > BLOCK_H:
+        VALID_BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr = BLOCK_H
+    else:
+        VALID_BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr = kv_group_num
+
+    cur_head = cur_head_id * VALID_BLOCK_H + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_H)
+    mask_h = cur_head < (cur_head_id + 1) * VALID_BLOCK_H
+    mask_h = mask_h & (cur_head < q_head_num)
+
+    offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_DMODEL)
+    offs_dv = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_DV)
+    mask_d = offs_d < HEAD_DIM
+    mask_dv = offs_dv < HEAD_DIM
+
+    cur_batch_seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens + cur_batch)
+
+    # Load Q for this head group
+    offs_q = cur_batch * stride_qb + cur_head[:, None] * stride_qh + offs_d[None, :]
+    q = tl.load(Q + offs_q, mask=mask_h[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0)
+
+    # Determine this split's token range
+    kv_len_per_split = tl.cdiv(cur_batch_seq_len, NUM_KV_SPLITS)
+    split_kv_start = kv_len_per_split * split_kv_id
+    split_kv_end = tl.minimum(split_kv_start + kv_len_per_split, cur_batch_seq_len)
+
+    # Online softmax accumulators
+    e_max = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H], dtype=tl.float32) - float("inf")
+    e_sum = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H], dtype=tl.float32)
+    acc = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H, BLOCK_DV], dtype=tl.float32)
+
+    if split_kv_end > split_kv_start:
+        # Iterate over pages within this split
+        start_page = split_kv_start // PAGE_SIZE
+        end_page = (split_kv_end + PAGE_SIZE - 1) // PAGE_SIZE
+
+        offs_token_in_page = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)
+        offs_dim = tl.arange(0, 2 * HEAD_DIM)
+
+        for page_idx in range(start_page, end_page):
+            physical_page = tl.load(
+                block_table + cur_batch * stride_bt0 + page_idx * stride_bt1,
+            )
+
+            # Global token indices for this page
+            global_token_idx = page_idx * PAGE_SIZE + offs_token_in_page
+            token_mask = global_token_idx < split_kv_end
+
+            # Base address for this page and KV head
+            page_base = (
+                KV_Cache
+                + physical_page * stride_kv0
+                + cur_kv_head * stride_kv2
+            )
+
+            # Load full page: (PAGE_SIZE, 2*HEAD_DIM)
+            page_data = tl.load(
+                page_base + offs_token_in_page[:, None] * stride_kv1 + offs_dim[None, :],
+                mask=token_mask[:, None],
+                other=0.0,
+            )
+
+            # Extract K and V
+            k = page_data[:, :HEAD_DIM]  # (PAGE_SIZE, HEAD_DIM)
+            v = page_data[:, HEAD_DIM:]  # (PAGE_SIZE, HEAD_DIM)
+
+            # Compute QK^T
+            qk = tl.dot(q, k.to(q.dtype).T)
+            qk *= sm_scale
+
+            # Mask tokens beyond split end or seq_len
+            qk = tl.where(
+                mask_h[:, None] & token_mask[None, :],
+                qk,
+                float("-inf"),
+            )
+
+            # Online softmax update
+            n_e_max = tl.maximum(tl.max(qk, 1), e_max)
+            re_scale = tl.exp(e_max - n_e_max)
+            p = tl.exp(qk - n_e_max[:, None])
+
+            acc *= re_scale[:, None]
+            acc += tl.dot(p.to(v.dtype), v)
+
+            e_sum = e_sum * re_scale + tl.sum(p, 1)
+            e_max = n_e_max
+
+        # Store partial output and LSE
+        offs_mid_o = (
+            cur_batch * stride_mid_ob
+            + cur_head[:, None] * stride_mid_oh
+            + split_kv_id * stride_mid_os
+            + offs_dv[None, :]
+        )
+        tl.store(
+            Mid_O + offs_mid_o,
+            acc / e_sum[:, None],
+            mask=mask_h[:, None] & mask_dv[None, :],
+        )
+
+        offs_mid_lse = (
+            cur_batch * stride_mid_ob
+            + cur_head * stride_mid_oh
+            + split_kv_id * stride_mid_os
+            + HEAD_DIM
+        )
+        tl.store(
+            Mid_LSE + offs_mid_lse,
+            e_max + tl.log(e_sum),
+

Actually, Triton uses a "blocked" layout. For a tensor of shape (M, N), threads are arranged in a 2D grid. The exact mapping depends on the tensor layout. For `tl.load` of shape (16, 128) with 128 threads: - The tensor is divided into blocks, and each thread handles one or more elements. - Typically, for a row-major layout, threads in a warp access contiguous elements in the row dimension. If warp 0 handles row 0, elements 0..31 (assuming 32 threads per warp), then: - Thread 0: (0, 0) - Thread 1: (0, 1) - ... - Thread 31: (0, 31) This accesses addresses page_base+0, page_base+1, ..., page_base+31. The memory controller can handle this, but it's not as efficient as contiguous access. For K only (16 * 128 = 2048 elements = 4096 bytes), we're loading about 4096 bytes. import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '.')
import torch
import reference
import solution
import shapes

def apply_shape(shape):
    reference.BATCH = shape["batch"]
    reference.NUM_HEADS = shape["num_heads"]
    reference.NUM_KV_HEADS = shape["num_kv_heads"]
    reference.HEAD_DIM = shape["head_dim"]
    reference.SEQ_LEN = shape["seq_len"]
    reference.PAGE_SIZE = shape["page_size"]

device = torch.device("cuda:0")

for shape_idx, shape in enumerate(shapes.SHAPES):
    apply_shape(shape)
    init_args = reference.get_init_inputs()
    ref_model = reference.Model(*init_args).to(device).eval()
    sol_model = solution.Model(*init_args).to(device).eval()
    
    torch.manual_seed(42)
    inputs = [t.to(device) for t in reference.get_inputs()]
    
    # Warmup
    for _ in range(5):
        sol_model(*inputs)
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    
    # Time it
    import time
    start = time.perf_counter()
    for _ in range(30):
        sol_model(*inputs)
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    elapsed = (time.perf_counter() - start) / 30 * 1000
    
    print(f"shape={shape_idx} {shape} ms={elapsed:.3f}")
EOF

"""Centralized GPU timing for benchmark.py files.

All problems' benchmark.py should call `time_fn` from here so we have one
implementation of warmup, L2 flush, and CUDA event capture to maintain.

Methodology:
  - 10 warmup calls absorb Triton autotune (typical ~7 configs) and
    torch.compile reduce-overhead CUDA-graph capture.
  - Between each timed call, `_l2_flush()` writes 128 MB to evict L2
    (Blackwell L2 is 96 MB; we want any prior L2 contents flushed so
    we measure HBM-load bandwidth, not L2-cached bandwidth).
  - GPU timing via cuda.Event with synchronize() AFTER record() but
    BEFORE elapsed_time() — the canonical NVIDIA pattern.
  - Reported value is the median of `iters` trials, robust to outliers.

Notes / known biases not addressed here:
  - torch.compile(mode="reduce-overhead") gets CUDA graphs which eliminate
    launch overhead. Custom Triton/CUDA kernels do NOT get this treatment.
    On small shapes where launch overhead matters, this gives compile an
    artificial advantage. We accept this as the cost of using the agreed
    "compiled" baseline policy.
  - cuBLAS / cuDNN allocate workspaces on first call. 10 warmup absorbs.
  - Median over a fairly small number of trials (default 30) is fine for
    headline numbers but won't catch bimodal distributions. Use --extra
    instrumentation if you ever care.
"""

import statistics

Actually, Triton with 128 threads loading (16, 128): - Each thread might handle multiple elements. - The exact mapping is determined by Triton's layout system. - But in general, threads in a warp access contiguous elements. For a block of shape (16, 128), Triton might use a layout like `(4, 32)` or `(8, 16)` for the thread arrangement. The key is that a warp accesses a contiguous sub-block. If a warp accesses a 1x32 sub-block (32 elements in one row), then: - Warp 0: row 0, elements 0..31 -> indices 0..31, coalesced - Warp 1: row 0, elements 32..63 -> indices 32..63, coalesced - Warp 2: row 0, elements 64..95 -> indices 64..95, coalesced - Warp 3: row 0, elements 96..127 -> indices 96..127, coalesced - Warp 4: row 1, elements 0..31 -> indices 2048..2079, coalesced but 8192 bytes from previous With 4 warps (128 threads), it takes 4 iterations to load row 0. Then another 4 iterations to load row 1, etc. Total 64 iterations for the full (16, 128) block. Wait, that can't be right. Triton vectorizes loads. With 128 threads, each thread might load 16 elements using vectorized loads. So the total number of load instructions is much smaller. Actually, Triton automatically determines the vector width based on the data type and alignment. For bf16, it might use 8-element vectors (128 bits). With 128 threads, each loading 8 elements, a (16, 128) block requires 2 instructions per thread = 256 elements total per instruction * 128 threads = 32,768 elements... no wait. Let me think differently. A (16, 128) block has 2048 elements. With 128 threads, if each thread loads 16 elements, that's 1 instruction per thread. Triton figures this out. The key insight is: Triton with vectorized loads can load a (16, 128) block very efficiently if the elements are contiguous in memory. But our elements are NOT contiguous across rows. For row 0, elements 0..127 are contiguous. For row 1, elements 0..127 are contiguous but 2048 elements away. A vectorized load for row 1 cannot be combined with row 0. So the memory controller issues separate transactions for each row. With 16 rows, we need at least 16 separate memory transactions for K (one per row). Each transaction is 128 elements * 2 bytes = 256 bytes. Total = 4096 bytes. This is the same as the data size, so we're not loading extra bytes. But the 16 separate transactions might not fully utilize the memory bus. For comparison, if K were stored contiguously for all 16 tokens (16*128=2048 elements), it would be one contiguous 4096-byte chunk. The memory controller could load this in a few large transactions (e.g., 4 x 1024-byte transactions). This is much more efficient. So the strided layout does hurt performance, but not by reading extra data - it hurts by fragmenting the memory transactions. For D=64, the effect is similar but each row is smaller (128 elements = 256 bytes). cat > /tmp/test_blockh.py << 'EOF'
import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def test_kernel(Q, K, Out, BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_N: tl.constexpr):
    offs_h = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_H)
    offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)
    q = tl.load(Q + offs_h[:, None] * BLOCK_D + offs_d[None, :])
    k = tl.load(K + offs_d[:, None] * BLOCK_N + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_N)[None, :])
    out = tl.dot(q, k)
    tl.store(Out + offs_h[:, None] * BLOCK_N + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_N)[None, :], out)

Q = torch.randn(4, 128, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device='cuda')
K = torch.randn(128, 16, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device='cuda')
Out = torch.empty(4, 16, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device='cuda')

test_kernel[(1,)](Q, K, Out, BLOCK_H=4, BLOCK_D=128, BLOCK_N=16)
print("BLOCK_H=4 works!")

test_kernel[(1,)](Q, K, Out, BLOCK_H=8, BLOCK_D=128, BLOCK_N=16)
print("BLOCK_H=8 works!")
EOF

This requires a physical reordering of the data. So there's no way around it without a copy. The packed layout fundamentally stores tokens strided by `num_kv_heads * 2 * head_dim`. import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def test_kernel(Q, K, Out, BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_N: tl.constexpr):
    offs_h = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_H)
    offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)
    q = tl.load(Q + offs_h[:, None] * BLOCK_D + offs_d[None, :])
    k = tl.load(K + offs_d[:, None] * BLOCK_N + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_N)[None, :])
    out = tl.dot(q, k)
    tl.store(Out + offs_h[:, None] * BLOCK_N + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_N)[None, :], out)

Q = torch.randn(1, 128, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device='cuda')
K = torch.randn(128, 16, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device='cuda')
Out = torch.empty(1, 16, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device='cuda')

test_kernel[(1,)](Q, K, Out, BLOCK_H=1, BLOCK_D=128, BLOCK_N=16)
print("BLOCK_H=1 works!")

    reference.NUM_KV_HEADS = shape["num_kv_heads"]
    reference.HEAD_DIM = shape["head_dim"]

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '.')
import torch
import reference
import solution
import shapes
import triton

def apply_shape(shape):
    reference.BATCH = shape["batch"]
    reference.NUM_HEADS = shape["num_heads"]
    reference.NUM_KV_HEADS = shape["num_kv_heads"]
    reference.HEAD_DIM = shape["head_dim"]
    reference.SEQ_LEN = shape["seq_len"]
    reference.PAGE_SIZE = shape["page_size"]

device = torch.device("cuda:0")

# Test shape 0 and shape 4
for shape_idx in [0, 4]:
    shape = shapes.SHAPES[shape_idx]
    apply_shape(shape)
    init_args = reference.get_init_inputs()
    sol_model = solution.Model(*init_args).to(device).eval()
    
    torch.manual_seed(42)
    inputs = [t.to(device) for t in reference.get_inputs()]
    
    # Warmup
    for _ in range(10):
        sol_model(*inputs)
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    
    # Time with L2 flush
    _l2_scratch = torch.empty(128 * 1024 * 1024 // 4, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")
    
    times = []
    for _ in range(30):
        _l2_scratch.zero_()
        torch.cuda.synchronize()
        s = torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True)
        e = torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True)
        s.record()
        sol_model(*inputs)
        e.record()
        torch.cuda.synchronize()
        times.append(s.elapsed_time(e))
    
    import statistics
    print(f"shape={shape_idx} baseline ms={statistics.median(times):.3f}")
EOF

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '.')
import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl
import reference
import shapes

def apply_shape(shape):
    reference.BATCH = shape["batch"]
    reference.NUM_HEADS = shape["num_heads"]
    reference.NUM_KV_HEADS = shape["num_kv_heads"]
    reference.HEAD_DIM = shape["head_dim"]
    reference.SEQ_LEN = shape["seq_len"]
    reference.PAGE_SIZE = shape["page_size"]

# Copy the kernel and modify parameters
device = torch.device("cuda:0")
shape = shapes.SHAPES[0]
apply_shape(shape)
init_args = reference.get_init_inputs()

# Import solution to get the kernel code
import solution

# Time the current solution
sol_model = solution.Model(*init_args).to(device).eval()
torch.manual_seed(42)
inputs = [t.to(device) for t in reference.get_inputs()]

for _ in range(10):
    sol_model(*inputs)
torch.cuda.synchronize()

_l2_scratch = torch.empty(128 * 1024 * 1024 // 4, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")

times = []
for _ in range(30):
    _l2_scratch.zero_()
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    s = torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True)
    e = torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True)
    s.record()
    sol_model(*inputs)
    e.record()
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    times.append(s.elapsed_time(e))

import statistics
print(f"Current: ms={statistics.median(times):.3f}")

Let me try a different approach. I'll write a more optimized Triton kernel that: 1. Uses `BLOCK_N = 64` or `128` tokens per iteration (instead of page-by-page) 2. Loads K and V efficiently from the packed layout by using a gather strategy 3. Uses a single stage when possible Actually, I realize that the packed layout problem is the main bottleneck. Let me try to restructure the loads. For the packed layout, if I load K for BLOCK_N tokens, each token's K is spaced by `num_kv_heads * 2 * head_dim`. For Hkv=8, D=128, this is 2048 elements = 4096 bytes. What if I transpose the load? Instead of loading K as (BLOCK_N, HEAD_DIM), I can load it as (HEAD_DIM, BLOCK_N) by having each thread load one element of K for all BLOCK_N tokens. ```python # For d in 0..HEAD_DIM-1, load K[d] for all tokens # Address for token t, dim d: base + t * stride_kv1 + d ``` In Triton, if I use `tl.load` with shape (HEAD_DIM, BLOCK_N): - Thread (d, t) accesses base + t * stride_kv1 + d - A warp of 32 threads accesses 32 consecutive t values for the same d - These are spaced by stride_kv1 = 4096 bytes - Terrible coalescing What if I load the full token data (K+V) for BLOCK_N tokens as a flat array? For BLOCK_N=16 (one page), the data is 16 * 256 = 4096 elements = 8192 bytes. I can load this as a 1D array and then extract K and V. In Triton: ```python # Load page as flat 1D array page_data_1d = tl.load(page_base + tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE * 2 * HEAD_DIM)) # Reshape to (PAGE_SIZE, 2*HEAD_DIM) page_data = tl.reshape(page_data_1d, (PAGE_SIZE, 2 * HEAD_DIM)) k = page_data[:, :HEAD_DIM] v = page_data[:, HEAD_DIM:] ``` But `tl.reshape` from 1D to 2D might work differently. Let me check if Triton supports this. Actually, `tl.reshape` should support any valid reshape. But does it create a copy or a view? In Triton, reshapes are typically views on the same data. But wait, `page_base + tl.arange(0, N)` loads N contiguous elements. For one page, these are exactly all the K+V data for all tokens in that page. This is perfectly coalesced! Then `tl.reshape(page_data_1d, (PAGE_SIZE, 2 * HEAD_DIM))` gives a 2D view where `page_data[token, dim]` accesses the right element. And `k = page_data[:, :HEAD_DIM]` extracts K. This approach avoids the strided load issue entirely! Instead of loading K with stride 4096 between rows, I load the entire page contiguously and then slice. But earlier I tried `page_data[:, :HEAD_DIM]` and Triton gave an error: "unsupported tensor index". That was with Triton 3.6. What if I use `tl.reshape` to extract K and V? ```python page_data_1d = tl.load(page_base + tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE * 2 * HEAD_DIM), ...) # Reshape to (PAGE_SIZE, 2, HEAD_DIM) page_3d = tl.reshape(page_data_1d, (PAGE_SIZE, 2, HEAD_DIM)) k = page_3d[:, 0, :] # (PAGE_SIZE, HEAD_DIM) v = page_3d[:, 1, :] # (PAGE_SIZE, HEAD_DIM) ``` Would this work? The physical layout of `page_data_1d` is: ``` [t0_K0, t0_K1, ..., t0_K127, t0_V0, t0_V1, ..., t0_V127, t1_K0, t1_K1, ..., t1_K127, t1_V0, t1_V1, ..., t1_V127, ...] ``` If I reshape this to (PAGE_SIZE, 2, HEAD_DIM): - page_3d[0, 0, :] = [t0_K0, ..., t0_K127] ✓ - page_3d[0, 1, :] = [t0_V0, ..., t0_V127] ✓ - page_3d[1, 0, :] = [t1_K0, ..., t1_K127] ✓ Yes! This is exactly the layout we want. So: 1. Load `PAGE_SIZE * 2 * HEAD_DIM` contiguous elements 2. Reshape to `(PAGE_SIZE, 2, HEAD_DIM)` 3. Extract K and V This should be much more efficient than strided loads! But does Triton support `tl.reshape` in kernels? And can it be used with slices? Let me test this. Actually, I realize there might be an issue with `tl.reshape` on loaded data. In Triton, `tl.load` returns a block tensor. `tl.reshape` might require the total number of elements to be the same, which it is. But the exact semantics might depend on the Triton version. Let me test this approach with a simple kernel.

cat > /tmp/test_reshape.py << 'EOF'
import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def test_kernel(KV, K_Out, V_Out, PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr, HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr):
    page_base = KV + tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE * 2 * HEAD_DIM)
    page_data = tl.load(page_base)
    # Try reshape to (PAGE_SIZE, 2, HEAD_DIM)
    page_3d = tl.reshape(page_data, (PAGE_SIZE, 2, HEAD_DIM))
    k = page_3d[:, 0, :]
    v = page_3d[:, 1, :]
    
    # Store to verify
    k_flat = tl.reshape(k, (PAGE_SIZE * HEAD_DIM,))
    v_flat = tl.reshape(v, (PAGE_SIZE * HEAD_DIM,))
    tl.store(K_Out + tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE * HEAD_DIM), k_flat)
    tl.store(V_Out + tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE * HEAD_DIM), v_flat)

PAGE_SIZE = 16
HEAD_DIM = 128

kv = torch.randn(PAGE_SIZE, 2, HEAD_DIM, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device='cuda')
# Flatten to simulate packed layout: (PAGE_SIZE, 2*HEAD_DIM)
kv_packed = kv.view(PAGE_SIZE, 2 * HEAD_DIM)

k_out = torch.empty(PAGE_SIZE * HEAD_DIM, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device='cuda')
v_out = torch.empty(PAGE_SIZE * HEAD_DIM, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device='cuda')

test_kernel[(1,)](kv_packed, k_out, v_out, PAGE_SIZE=PAGE_SIZE, HEAD_DIM=HEAD_DIM)

k_expected = kv[:, 0, :].reshape(-1)
v_expected = kv[:, 1, :].reshape(-1)

print("K match:", torch.allclose(k_out, k_expected, atol=1e-5))
print("V match:", torch.allclose(v_out, v_expected, atol=1e-5))

import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def test_kernel(KV, K_Out, V_Out, PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr, HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr):
    n = PAGE_SIZE * 2 * HEAD_DIM
    page_data = tl.load(KV + tl.arange(0, n))
    
    # Build 2D indices for K
    offs_t = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)[:, None]
    offs_d = tl.arange(0, HEAD_DIM)[None, :]
    idx_k = offs_t * (2 * HEAD_DIM) + offs_d
    k = page_data[idx_k]
    
    idx_v = offs_t * (2 * HEAD_DIM) + offs_d + HEAD_DIM
    v = page_data[idx_v]
    
    # Flatten and store
    tl.store(K_Out + tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE * HEAD_DIM), tl.reshape(k, (PAGE_SIZE * HEAD_DIM,)))
    tl.store(V_Out + tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE * HEAD_DIM), tl.reshape(v, (PAGE_SIZE * HEAD_DIM,)))

PAGE_SIZE = 16
HEAD_DIM = 128

kv = torch.randn(PAGE_SIZE, 2, HEAD_DIM, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device='cuda')
kv_packed = kv.view(PAGE_SIZE * 2 * HEAD_DIM)

k_out = torch.empty(PAGE_SIZE * HEAD_DIM, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device='cuda')
v_out = torch.empty(PAGE_SIZE * HEAD_DIM, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device='cuda')

test_kernel[(1,)](kv_packed, k_out, v_out, PAGE_SIZE=PAGE_SIZE, HEAD_DIM=HEAD_DIM)

k_expected = kv[:, 0, :].reshape(-1)
v_expected = kv[:, 1, :].reshape(-1)

print("K match:", torch.allclose(k_out, k_expected, atol=1e-5))
print("V match:", torch.allclose(v_out, v_expected, atol=1e-5))

import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def test_kernel(KV, K_Out, V_Out, PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr, HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr):
    total: tl.constexpr = PAGE_SIZE * 2 * HEAD_DIM
    page_data = tl.load(KV + tl.arange(0, total))
    
    # Build 2D indices for K
    offs_t = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)[:, None]
    offs_d = tl.arange(0, HEAD_DIM)[None, :]
    idx_k = offs_t * (2 * HEAD_DIM) + offs_d
    k = page_data[idx_k]
    
    idx_v = offs_t * (2 * HEAD_DIM) + offs_d + HEAD_DIM
    v = page_data[idx_v]
    
    # Flatten and store
    k_total: tl.constexpr = PAGE_SIZE * HEAD_DIM
    tl.store(K_Out + tl.arange(0, k_total), tl.reshape(k, (k_total,)))
    tl.store(V_Out + tl.arange(0, k_total), tl.reshape(v, (k_total,)))

PAGE_SIZE = 16
HEAD_DIM = 128

kv = torch.randn(PAGE_SIZE, 2, HEAD_DIM, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device='cuda')
kv_packed = kv.view(PAGE_SIZE * 2 * HEAD_DIM)

k_out = torch.empty(PAGE_SIZE * HEAD_DIM, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device='cuda')
v_out = torch.empty(PAGE_SIZE * HEAD_DIM, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device='cuda')

test_kernel[(1,)](kv_packed, k_out, v_out, PAGE_SIZE=PAGE_SIZE, HEAD_DIM=HEAD_DIM)

k_expected = kv[:, 0, :].reshape(-1)
v_expected = kv[:, 1, :].reshape(-1)

print("K match:", torch.allclose(k_out, k_expected, atol=1e-5))
print("V match:", torch.allclose(v_out, v_expected, atol=1e-5))

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '.')
import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl
import reference
import shapes
import math

def apply_shape(shape):
    reference.BATCH = shape["batch"]
    reference.NUM_HEADS = shape["num_heads"]
    reference.NUM_KV_HEADS = shape["num_kv_heads"]
    reference.HEAD_DIM = shape["head_dim"]
    reference.SEQ_LEN = shape["seq_len"]
    reference.PAGE_SIZE = shape["page_size"]

# Kernel variants
@triton.jit
def _fwd_kernel_stage1_v2(
    Q,
    KV_Cache,
    block_table,
    seq_lens,
    sm_scale,
    Mid_O,
    stride_qb,
    stride_qh,
    stride_bt0,
    stride_bt1,
    stride_kv0,
    stride_kv1,
    stride_kv2,
    stride_kv3,
    stride_mid_ob,
    stride_mid_oh,
    stride_mid_os,
    kv_group_num: tl.constexpr,
    q_head_num: tl.constexpr,
    BLOCK_DMODEL: tl.constexpr,
    BLOCK_DV: tl.constexpr,
    BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr,
    NUM_KV_SPLITS: tl.constexpr,
    PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
    HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
):
    cur_batch = tl.program_id(0)
    cur_head_id = tl.program_id(1)
    split_kv_id = tl.program_id(2)

    heads_per_kv = tl.cdiv(kv_group_num, BLOCK_H)
    cur_kv_head = cur_head_id // heads_per_kv

    if kv_group_num > BLOCK_H:
        VALID_BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr = BLOCK_H
    else:
        VALID_BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr = kv_group_num

    cur_head = cur_head_id * VALID_BLOCK_H + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_H)
    mask_h = cur_head < (cur_head_id + 1) * VALID_BLOCK_H
    mask_h = mask_h & (cur_head < q_head_num)

    offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_DMODEL)
    offs_dv = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_DV)
    mask_d = offs_d < HEAD_DIM
    mask_dv = offs_dv < HEAD_DIM

    cur_batch_seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens + cur_batch)

    offs_q = cur_batch * stride_qb + cur_head[:, None] * stride_qh + offs_d[None, :]
    q = tl.load(Q + offs_q, mask=mask_h[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0)

    kv_len_per_split = tl.cdiv(cur_batch_seq_len, NUM_KV_SPLITS)
    split_kv_start = kv_len_per_split * split_kv_id
    split_kv_end = tl.minimum(split_kv_start + kv_len_per_split, cur_batch_seq_len)

    e_max = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H], dtype=tl.float32) - float("inf")
    e_sum = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H], dtype=tl.float32)
    acc = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H, BLOCK_DV], dtype=tl.float32)

    if split_kv_end > split_kv_start:
        start_page = split_kv_start // PAGE_SIZE
        end_page = (split_kv_end + PAGE_SIZE - 1) // PAGE_SIZE

        offs_token_in_page = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)

        for page_idx in range(start_page, end_page):
            physical_page = tl.load(
                block_table + cur_batch * stride_bt0 + page_idx * stride_bt1,
            )

            global_token_idx = page_idx * PAGE_SIZE + offs_token_in_page
            token_mask = global_token_idx < split_kv_end

            page_base = (
                KV_Cache
                + physical_page * stride_kv0
                + cur_kv_head * stride_kv2
            )

            k = tl.load(
                page_base + offs_token_in_page[:, None] * stride_kv1 + offs_d[None, :],
                mask=token_mask[:, None] & mask_d[None, :],
                other=0.0,
            )
            v = tl.load(
                page_base + offs_token_in_page[:, None] * stride_kv1 + (HEAD_DIM + offs_dv)[None, :],
                mask=token_mask[:, None] & mask_dv[None, :],
                other=0.0,
            )

            qk = tl.dot(q, k.to(q.dtype).T)
            qk *= sm_scale
            qk = tl.where(
                mask_h[:, None] & token_mask[None, :],
                qk,
                float("-inf"),
            )

            n_e_max = tl.maximum(tl.max(qk, 1), e_max)
            re_scale = tl.exp(e_max - n_e_max)
            p = tl.exp(qk - n_e_max[:, None])

            acc *= re_scale[:, None]
            acc += tl.dot(p.to(v.dtype), v)

            e_sum = e_sum * re_scale + tl.sum(p, 1)
            e_max = n_e_max

        offs_mid_o = (
            cur_batch * stride_mid_ob
            + cur_head[:

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '.')
import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl
import reference
import math

shape = {"batch": 8, "num_heads": 32, "num_kv_heads": 8, "head_dim": 128, "seq_len": 1024, "page_size": 16}
B, H, Hkv, D, L, P = shape["batch"], shape["num_heads"], shape["num_kv_heads"], shape["head_dim"], shape["seq_len"], shape["page_size"]

device = torch.device("cuda:0")
pages_per_seq = (L + P - 1) // P
total_pages = max(B * pages_per_seq + 8, 64)

query = torch.randn(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=device) * 0.1
kv_cache = torch.randn(total_pages, P, Hkv, 2 * D, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=device) * 0.1
block_table = torch.randperm(total_pages)[:B * pages_per_seq].reshape(B, pages_per_seq).int().to(device)
seq_lens = torch.full((B,), L, dtype=torch.int32, device=device)

ref_model = reference.Model(B, H, Hkv, D, L, P).to(device).eval()
with torch.no_grad():
    ref_out = ref_model(query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens)

# Import the sweep kernel
import importlib.util
spec = importlib.util.spec_from_file_location("sweep", "/tmp/sweep_blockh.py")

# Actually, just run the kernel directly using the code from sweep
@triton.jit
def _fwd_kernel_stage1_v2(
    Q, KV_Cache, block_table, seq_lens, sm_scale, Mid_O,
    stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_bt0, stride_bt1,
    stride_kv0, stride_kv1, stride_kv2, stride_kv3,
    stride_mid_ob, stride_mid_oh, stride_mid_os,
    kv_group_num: tl.constexpr, q_head_num: tl.constexpr,
    BLOCK_DMODEL: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_DV: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr,
    NUM_KV_SPLITS: tl.constexpr, PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr, HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
):
    cur_batch = tl.program_id(0)
    cur_head_id = tl.program_id(1)
    split_kv_id = tl.program_id(2)
    heads_per_kv = tl.cdiv(kv_group_num, BLOCK_H)
    cur_kv_head = cur_head_id // heads_per_kv
    if kv_group_num > BLOCK_H:
        VALID_BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr = BLOCK_H
    else:
        VALID_BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr = kv_group_num
    cur_head = cur_head_id * VALID_BLOCK_H + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_H)
    mask_h = cur_head < (cur_head_id + 1) * VALID_BLOCK_H
    mask_h = mask_h & (cur_head < q_head_num)
    offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_DMODEL)
    offs_dv = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_DV)
    mask_d = offs_d < HEAD_DIM
    mask_dv = offs_dv < HEAD_DIM
    cur_batch_seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens + cur_batch)
    offs_q = cur_batch * stride_qb + cur_head[:, None] * stride_qh + offs_d[None, :]
    q = tl.load(Q + offs_q, mask=mask_h[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0)
    kv_len_per_split = tl.cdiv(cur_batch_seq_len, NUM_KV_SPLITS)
    split_kv_start = kv_len_per_split * split_kv_id
    split_kv_end = tl.minimum(split_kv_start + kv_len_per_split, cur_batch_seq_len)
    e_max = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H], dtype=tl.float32) - float("inf")
    e_sum = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H], dtype=tl.float32)
    acc = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H, BLOCK_DV], dtype=tl.float32)
    if split_kv_end > split_kv_start:
        start_page = split_kv_start // PAGE_SIZE
        end_page = (split_kv_end + PAGE_SIZE - 1) // PAGE_SIZE
        offs_token_in_page = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)
        for page_idx in range(start_page, end_page):
            physical_page = tl.load(block_table + cur_batch * stride_bt0 + page_idx * stride_bt1)
            global_token_idx = page_idx * PAGE_SIZE + offs_token_in_page
            token_mask = global_token_idx < split_kv_end
            page_base = KV_Cache + physical_page * stride_kv0 + cur_kv_head * stride_kv2
            k = tl.load(page_base + offs_token_in_page[:, None] * stride_kv1 + offs_d[None, :],
                        mask=token_mask[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0)
            v = tl.load(page_base + offs_token_in_page[:, None] * stride_kv1 + (HEAD_DIM + offs_dv)[None, :],
                        mask=token_mask[:, None] & mask_dv[None, :], other=0.0)
            qk = tl.dot(q, k.to(q.dtype).T)
            qk *= sm_scale
            qk = tl.where(mask_h[:, None] & token_mask[None, :], qk, float("-inf"))

With BLOCK_H=16 and grid_y=2: - Block 0 processes heads 0..3 correctly, but heads 4..15 output zero - Block 1 processes heads 16..19 (but with KV head 1 instead of 4), and heads 20..31 output zero So heads 4..15 and 20..31 are zero! Heads 16..19 use the wrong KV head! But in my earlier sweep, the max_diff was reported as 0.0001. That was because my sweep script had a bug in the correctness check - it was running the kernel once for correctness and then a second time for timing, and the second run might have overwritten the output. Or there was some caching issue. Anyway, the key finding is: BLOCK_H MUST be <= kv_group_num, or the grid_y must be computed as `cdiv(head_num, min(BLOCK_H, kv_group_num))`. So using BLOCK_H=16 for group_size=4 is WRONG unless grid_y=8. But wait, if I use grid_y = cdiv(head_num, min(BLOCK_H, kv_group_num)) = cdiv(32, 4) = 8 with BLOCK_H=16, then: - Block 0: heads 0..15, valid=0..3, KV head 0 - Block 1: heads 4..19, valid=4..7, KV head 1 - ... - Block 7: heads 28..43, valid=28..31, KV head 7 This is correct! Each block processes one KV head's worth of query heads. And the total number of blocks is the same as with BLOCK_H=4! So using BLOCK_H=16 with the correct grid gives the same block count as BLOCK_H=4. Then why was BLOCK_H=16 with splits=8 giving 0.034 ms for shape 0 while BLOCK_H=4 with splits=8 gave 0.044 ms? In my sweep, BLOCK_H=16 used grid_y=2, not 8. So it launched fewer blocks, did less work, and was faster because it produced wrong results! This explains everything. The "fast" configurations in my sweep with BLOCK_H=16 were actually wrong. OK so the real comparison is: - BLOCK_H=4, splits=8: 0.044 ms (correct) - BLOCK_H=8, splits=8: 0.038 ms (but shape 0 has group_size=4, so BLOCK_H=8 is also wrong unless grid_y=8) Wait, BLOCK_H=8 with group_size=4: - grid_y = cdiv(32, min(8, 4)) = cdiv(32, 4) = 8 - Block 0: heads 0..7, valid=0..3, KV head 0 - Block 1: heads 4..11, valid=4..7, KV head 1 This is correct! So BLOCK_H can be any multiple of the group size, as long as grid_y = cdiv(head_num, min(BLOCK_H, kv_group_num)). Wait, but if BLOCK_H > kv_group_num, then `VALID_BLOCK_H = kv_group_num`. Each block processes `kv_group_num` valid heads. The `tl.dot` has `BLOCK_H` rows but only `kv_group_num` are non-zero. This wastes tensor core capacity. For BLOCK_H=8 and kv_group_num=4: - `tl.dot((8, 128), (128, 16))` but only 4 rows are non-zero - 50% tensor core waste For BLOCK_H=16 and kv_group_num=4: - `tl.dot((16, 128), (128, 16))` but only 4 rows are non-zero - 75% tensor core waste But the grid_y is the same (8) regardless of BLOCK_H. So the block count is the same. The only difference is tensor core utilization. So BLOCK_H=4 should be more efficient than BLOCK_H=8 or 16 for group_size=4. Then why did my sweep show BLOCK_H=8, splits=8 = 0.038 ms and BLOCK_H=4, splits=8 = 0.044 ms? Let me re-examine. In my sweep, for BLOCK_H=8, I used `grid = (batch, triton.cdiv(head_num, BLOCK_H), num_kv_splits)`. So grid_y = cdiv(32, 8) = 4. With group_size=4 and BLOCK_H=8: - Block 0: heads 0..7, valid=0..3, KV head 0 - Block 1: heads 8..15, valid=8..11, KV head 1... wait, head 8 should use KV head 2, not 1! `cur_kv_head = cur_head_id // cdiv(4, 8) = cur_head_id // 1 = cur_head_id` Block 1: cur_head_id=1, cur_kv_head=1. But heads 8..11 should use KV head 2! So BLOCK_H=8 with grid_y=4 is also wrong! The correct grid_y for any BLOCK_H when kv_group_num=4 is ALWAYS 8. Because there are 8 KV heads, and each KV head needs its own block. In vLLM's formula: ```python grid = ( batch, triton.cdiv(head_num, min(BLOCK_H, kv_group_num)), NUM_KV_SPLITS, ) ``` For head_num=32, kv_group_num=4, min(BLOCK_H, 4)=4, cdiv(32, 4)=8. So grid_y=8 is correct for ALL BLOCK_H values when kv_group_num=4. In my sweep script, I used `triton.cdiv(head_num, BLOCK_H)` instead of `triton.cdiv(head_num, min(BLOCK_H, kv_group_num))`. This was the bug! Let me re-run the sweep with the correct grid formula.

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '.')
import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl
import reference
import shapes
import math

def apply_shape(shape):
    reference.BATCH = shape["batch"]
    reference.NUM_HEADS = shape["num_heads"]
    reference.NUM_KV_HEADS = shape["num_kv_heads"]
    reference.HEAD_DIM = shape["head_dim"]
    reference.SEQ_LEN = shape["seq_len"]
    reference.PAGE_SIZE = shape["page_size"]

@triton.jit
def _fwd_kernel_stage1_v2(
    Q, KV_Cache, block_table, seq_lens, sm_scale, Mid_O,
    stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_bt0, stride_bt1,
    stride_kv0, stride_kv1, stride_kv2, stride_kv3,
    stride_mid_ob, stride_mid_oh, stride_mid_os,
    kv_group_num: tl.constexpr, q_head_num: tl.constexpr,
    BLOCK_DMODEL: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_DV: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr,
    NUM_KV_SPLITS: tl.constexpr, PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr, HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
):
    cur_batch = tl.program_id(0)
    cur_head_id = tl.program_id(1)
    split_kv_id = tl.program_id(2)
    heads_per_kv = tl.cdiv(kv_group_num, BLOCK_H)
    cur_kv_head = cur_head_id // heads_per_kv
    if kv_group_num > BLOCK_H:
        VALID_BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr = BLOCK_H
    else:
        VALID_BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr = kv_group_num
    cur_head = cur_head_id * VALID_BLOCK_H + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_H)
    mask_h = cur_head < (cur_head_id + 1) * VALID_BLOCK_H
    mask_h = mask_h & (cur_head < q_head_num)
    offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_DMODEL)
    offs_dv = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_DV)
    mask_d = offs_d < HEAD_DIM
    mask_dv = offs_dv < HEAD_DIM
    cur_batch_seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens + cur_batch)
    offs_q = cur_batch * stride_qb + cur_head[:, None] * stride_qh + offs_d[None, :]
    q = tl.load(Q + offs_q, mask=mask_h[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0)
    kv_len_per_split = tl.cdiv(cur_batch_seq_len, NUM_KV_SPLITS)
    split_kv_start = kv_len_per_split * split_kv_id
    split_kv_end = tl.minimum(split_kv_start + kv_len_per_split, cur_batch_seq_len)
    e_max = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H], dtype=tl.float32) - float("inf")
    e_sum = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H], dtype=tl.float32)
    acc = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H, BLOCK_DV], dtype=tl.float32)
    if split_kv_end > split_kv_start:
        start_page = split_kv_start // PAGE_SIZE
        end_page = (split_kv_end + PAGE_SIZE - 1) // PAGE_SIZE
        offs_token_in_page = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)
        for page_idx in range(start_page, end_page):
            physical_page = tl.load(block_table + cur_batch * stride_bt0 + page_idx * stride_bt1)
            global_token_idx = page_idx * PAGE_SIZE + offs_token_in_page
            token_mask = global_token_idx < split_kv_end
            page_base = KV_Cache + physical_page * stride_kv0 + cur_kv_head * stride_kv2
            k = tl.load(page_base + offs_token_in_page[:, None] * stride_kv1 + offs_d[None, :],
                        mask=token_mask[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0)
            v = tl.load(page_base + offs_token_in_page[:, None] * stride_kv1 + (HEAD_DIM + offs_dv)[None, :],
                        mask=token_mask[:, None] & mask_dv[None, :], other=0.0)
            qk = tl.dot(q, k.to(q.dtype).T)
            qk *= sm_scale
            qk = tl.where(mask_h[:, None] & token_mask[None, :], qk, float("-inf"))
            n_e_max = tl.maximum(tl.max(qk, 1), e_max)
            re_scale = tl.exp(e_max - n_e_max)
            p = tl.exp(qk - n_e_max[:, None])
            acc *= re_scale[:, None]
            acc += tl.dot(p.to(v.dtype), v)
            e_sum = e_sum * re_scale + tl.sum(p, 1)
            e_max = n_e_max
        offs_mid_o = cur_batch * stride_mid_ob + cur_head[:, None] * stride_mid_oh + split_kv_id * stride_mid_os + offs_dv[None, :]
        tl.store(Mid_O + offs_mid_o, acc / e_sum[:, None], mask=mask_h[:, None] & mask_dv[None, :])
        offs_mid_lse = cur_batch * stride_mid_ob + cur_head * stride_mid_oh + split_kv_id * stride_mid_os + HEAD_DIM
        tl.store(Mid_O + offs_mid_lse, e_max + tl.log(e_sum), mask=mask_h)

@tri

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '.')
import torch
import triton
import triton.language as tl
import reference
import shapes
import math

def apply_shape(shape):
    reference.BATCH = shape["batch"]
    reference.NUM_HEADS = shape["num_heads"]
    reference.NUM_KV_HEADS = shape["num_kv_heads"]
    reference.HEAD_DIM = shape["head_dim"]
    reference.SEQ_LEN = shape["seq_len"]
    reference.PAGE_SIZE = shape["page_size"]

@triton.jit
def _fwd_kernel_stage1_v2(
    Q, KV_Cache, block_table, seq_lens, sm_scale, Mid_O,
    stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_bt0, stride_bt1,
    stride_kv0, stride_kv1, stride_kv2, stride_kv3,
    stride_mid_ob, stride_mid_oh, stride_mid_os,
    kv_group_num: tl.constexpr, q_head_num: tl.constexpr,
    BLOCK_DMODEL: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_DV: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr,
    NUM_KV_SPLITS: tl.constexpr, PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr, HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
):
    cur_batch = tl.program_id(0)
    cur_head_id = tl.program_id(1)
    split_kv_id = tl.program_id(2)
    heads_per_kv = tl.cdiv(kv_group_num, BLOCK_H)
    cur_kv_head = cur_head_id // heads_per_kv
    if kv_group_num > BLOCK_H:
        VALID_BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr = BLOCK_H
    else:
        VALID_BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr = kv_group_num
    cur_head = cur_head_id * VALID_BLOCK_H + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_H)
    mask_h = cur_head < (cur_head_id + 1) * VALID_BLOCK_H
    mask_h = mask_h & (cur_head < q_head_num)
    offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_DMODEL)
    offs_dv = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_DV)
    mask_d = offs_d < HEAD_DIM
    mask_dv = offs_dv < HEAD_DIM
    cur_batch_seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens + cur_batch)
    offs_q = cur_batch * stride_qb + cur_head[:, None] * stride_qh + offs_d[None, :]
    q = tl.load(Q + offs_q, mask=mask_h[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0)
    kv_len_per_split = tl.cdiv(cur_batch_seq_len, NUM_KV_SPLITS)
    split_kv_start = kv_len_per_split * split_kv_id
    split_kv_end = tl.minimum(split_kv_start + kv_len_per_split, cur_batch_seq_len)
    e_max = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H], dtype=tl.float32) - float("inf")
    e_sum = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H], dtype=tl.float32)
    acc = tl.zeros([BLOCK_H, BLOCK_DV], dtype=tl.float32)
    if split_kv_end > split_kv_start:
        start_page = split_kv_start // PAGE_SIZE
        end_page = (split_kv_end + PAGE_SIZE - 1) // PAGE_SIZE
        offs_token_in_page = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)
        for page_idx in range(start_page, end_page):
            physical_page = tl.load(block_table + cur_batch * stride_bt0 + page_idx * stride_bt1)
            global_token_idx = page_idx * PAGE_SIZE + offs_token_in_page
            token_mask = global_token_idx < split_kv_end
            page_base = KV_Cache + physical_page * stride_kv0 + cur_kv_head * stride_kv2
            k = tl.load(page_base + offs_token_in_page[:, None] * stride_kv1 + offs_d[None, :],
                        mask=token_mask[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0)
            v = tl.load(page_base + offs_token_in_page[:, None] * stride_kv1 + (HEAD_DIM + offs_dv)[None, :],
                        mask=token_mask[:, None] & mask_dv[None, :], other=0.0)
            qk = tl.dot(q, k.to(q.dtype).T)
            qk *= sm_scale
            qk = tl.where(mask_h[:, None] & token_mask[None, :], qk, float("-inf"))
            n_e_max = tl.maximum(tl.max(qk, 1), e_max)
            re_scale = tl.exp(e_max - n_e_max)
            p = tl.exp(qk - n_e_max[:, None])
            acc *= re_scale[:, None]
            acc += tl.dot(p.to(v.dtype), v)
            e_sum = e_sum * re_scale + tl.sum(p, 1)
            e_max = n_e_max
        offs_mid_o = cur_batch * stride_mid_ob + cur_head[:, None] * stride_mid_oh + split_kv_id * stride_mid_os + offs_dv[None, :]
        tl.store(Mid_O + offs_mid_o, acc / e_sum[:, None], mask=mask_h[:, None] & mask_dv[None, :])
        offs_mid_lse = cur_batch * stride_mid_ob + cur_head * stride_mid_oh + split_kv_id * stride_mid_os + HEAD_DIM
        tl.store(Mid_O + offs_mid_lse, e_max + tl.log(e_sum), mask=mask_h)

The packed layout causes strided memory access. For each page of 16 tokens with D=64: - K is at offsets [0, 512, 1024, 1536, ...] (in bytes) - Wait, for D=64, num_kv_heads=4: - stride_kv1 = 4 * 2 * 64 = 512 elements = 1024 bytes - K for token 0: bytes [0, 127] - K for token 1: bytes [1024, 1151] - etc. A warp loading K for 16 tokens loads 16 chunks of 128 bytes, spaced 1024 bytes apart. The memory controller can handle this, but it's not fully efficient. For 16 tokens * 64 elements * 2 bytes = 2048 bytes of K data, we're issuing 16 separate 128-byte transactions. The GPU memory subsystem can coalesce some of these, but not all. On Blackwell, the L1 cache line is 128 bytes. Each K row is exactly 128 bytes. So loading 16 rows requires 16 cache line fetches. But these cache lines are spaced 1024 - 128 = 896 bytes apart. If the memory controller can fetch multiple cache lines in parallel, the effective bandwidth might still be decent. But 16 scattered lines per page is a lot. For comparison, if K were contiguous, loading 16 rows would require just 2 or 4 large transactions. This is the fundamental limitation of the packed layout. Without pre-processing or a custom gather kernel, we're stuck with this access pattern. Actually, wait. What if I process 32 tokens at a time by loading from 2 consecutive pages? The loop has half as many iterations, but each iteration does twice as much work. For small D where loop overhead matters, this might help.
